  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_663d1a91-ad81-4def-a17a-4f255d00f025'

<span id="freeTextContainer18337464087324863017"><div><b>This international bestseller is a sweeping portrait of motherhood, loss, and redemption in war-torn Sarajevo. </b><br/><br/> Filled with memories of the four-year siege of Sarajevo, Gemma reluctantly boards a flight from her native Rome to that war-scarred city with her sixteen-year-old son, Pietro. She hopes to teach her son about the city of his birth and about Diego, the father he n</div></span>
  <span id="freeText18337464087324863017" style="display:none"><div><b>This international bestseller is a sweeping portrait of motherhood, loss, and redemption in war-torn Sarajevo. </b><br /><br /> Filled with memories of the four-year siege of Sarajevo, Gemma reluctantly boards a flight from her native Rome to that war-scarred city with her sixteen-year-old son, Pietro. She hopes to teach her son about the city of his birth and about Diego, the father he never knew. Once there Gemma is caught between the present and the past, reliving her love affair with Diego, their determination to start a family, and their deep connection to Sarajevo even as the threat of war loomed.<br /><br /> In this haunting and sophisticated novel, Mazzantini masterfully probes the startling emotional territory of what makes a family-particularly what makes a mother. As the fate of Sarajevo converges with Gemma's all-consuming desire to have a child we see how far she is driven, in a stunning revelation that is both heartbreaking and cathartic.<br /><br /> Brought to life by an unforgettable cast of characters, <i>Twice Born</i> is a tale of the acts of brutality and generosity that war can inspire. A blockbuster bestseller in Mazzantini's native Italy, it has taken Europe by storm and will soon be published around the world.<br /><br /></div></span>
  <a data-text-id="18337464087324863017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1630079965127050290">I just told the plot of this novel out loud to my husband. And he listened. <br/>It leaves me with my heart pounding and a little bit broken. It takes turns I didn't always see coming. And it shows more clearly pictures of the Balkan war than the ones I saw with my own eyes on television and in the newspapers. (Isn't it often that way?)<br/>I'm wavering between 4 and 5 stars for it because some sections were a bit long-winded but in hindsight, what could be edited?<br/>You can talk about war. Or it can happen </span>
  <span id="freeText1630079965127050290" style="display:none">I just told the plot of this novel out loud to my husband. And he listened. <br />It leaves me with my heart pounding and a little bit broken. It takes turns I didn't always see coming. And it shows more clearly pictures of the Balkan war than the ones I saw with my own eyes on television and in the newspapers. (Isn't it often that way?)<br />I'm wavering between 4 and 5 stars for it because some sections were a bit long-winded but in hindsight, what could be edited?<br />You can talk about war. Or it can happen to you. This and more. <br />I won't say too much because, as usual, I think it's best not to know too much about a story before you read it. <br />Horrifying and beautiful, it'll take me a while to recover from this book. But I kind of hope I never really do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1630079965127050290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172341491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11481939516677401811">If this was an American story, it would only center around Gemma and Diego's relationship. Since it is a European story, it goes deeper and explores the boundaries and definitions of love, relationships, sex, and motherhood.<br/><br/>I almost don't know how to review this because it is translated and it's a story pertaining to a specific culture and backhistory - I noticed American goodreaders are rating this book lower. The writing is choppy which would normally be enough for me to stop reading. As a dif</span>
  <span id="freeText11481939516677401811" style="display:none">If this was an American story, it would only center around Gemma and Diego's relationship. Since it is a European story, it goes deeper and explores the boundaries and definitions of love, relationships, sex, and motherhood.<br /><br />I almost don't know how to review this because it is translated and it's a story pertaining to a specific culture and backhistory - I noticed American goodreaders are rating this book lower. The writing is choppy which would normally be enough for me to stop reading. As a different goodreader said, this book is very slow-paced. The protagonist isn't particularly likable, but some of the other characters come alive. I found myself smiling and getting emotionally invested in the relationship between Gemma and Diego. It's the kind of obsessive love we all want, and Mazzantini explores the the realities of such a relationship in the backdrop of a war. I don't think it's fair to rate the book lower because the story lost its puppy-love charm halfway through.<br /><br />This book is an emotional roller coaster and it could be difficult to keep reading - but I'm glad I did read until the final pages, because the ending is different from what one would assume 100 pages earlier.</span>

<div id="review_257897184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257897184" />
    <a title="CuteBadger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4084869-cutebadger"><img alt="CuteBadger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286982399p2/4084869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257897184?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CuteBadger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CuteBadger" href="/user/show/4084869-cutebadger">CuteBadger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781851688449" href="/book/show/12072451-twice-born">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257897184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9265162246262534529">An Italian woman returns to Sarajevo with her teenage son to revisit the places and people she and his father knew during the fighting there.<br/><br/>This was an incredibly intense read - I both wanted to read it and didn't want to read it at the same time as I was afraid I wouldn't be able to cope with learning what had gone on. I found myself reading in short bursts and having to steel myself to pick it up again each time I put it down. But it was so compelling that I absolutely <b>had</b> to get to the end, </span>
  <span id="freeText9265162246262534529" style="display:none">An Italian woman returns to Sarajevo with her teenage son to revisit the places and people she and his father knew during the fighting there.<br /><br />This was an incredibly intense read - I both wanted to read it and didn't want to read it at the same time as I was afraid I wouldn't be able to cope with learning what had gone on. I found myself reading in short bursts and having to steel myself to pick it up again each time I put it down. But it was so compelling that I absolutely <b>had</b> to get to the end, however difficult that was going to be.<br /><br />Right from the beginning of the novel there is a sense of unease, enough to let you know that Gemma's return to Sarajevo will uncover truths that we will find hard to deal with. The reader has a sketchy idea of what might have happened, but when the truth was revealed it was way beyond anything I could have imagined and was deeply shocking. While I had been expecting some of the revelations in the plot, a major occurence towards the end of the book completely blindsided me. It felt like so many terrible things had happened that there couldn't possibly be anything else to fear - how wrong could a reader be?<br /><br />As Gemma is an outsider in Sarajevo we see things through her eyes which means that the book doesn't much examine the causes of the conflict or look at the politics of it. We're shown it from an outsider's perspective, which is what we are too.<br /><br />As with all novels in translation it's hard to tell what comes from the novelist and what comes from the translator, but apart from a couple of places where American spelling and phrasing jarred me I wasn't aware of any awkwardness in the language. The way the book is written is quite rat-a-tat-tat - lots of short scenes interspersed with longer ones. It's quite filmic in a way, with lots of fast cuts.<br /><br />Saying I liked the book or enjoyed it doesn't really convey how I felt about it. It's an astonishing piece of work and it's something I'm glad I read, but I wouldn't want to put myself through it again.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9265162246262534529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_868727586" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/868727586" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1066511-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518107210p2/1066511.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/868727586?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/1066511-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Julie by: </span>
      Brion
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1066511-julie?shelf=munsonbook-theater">munsonbook-theater</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer868727586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8361809504824270910">Well.<br/><br/>This book was assigned to me by my brother for our two-person book club, and it's taken me quite a while to get through it. He advised me ahead of time that I would probably "either love it or hate it," but I fell a little short of that. I don't think I'd say I enjoyed it, but it had some interesting parts and the last 1/8 of the book made the rest of it more interesting - like watching the last half hour of The Shawshank Redemption.<br/><br/>The basic concept of the book - of Gemma and her son Pietr</span>
  <span id="freeText8361809504824270910" style="display:none">Well.<br /><br />This book was assigned to me by my brother for our two-person book club, and it's taken me quite a while to get through it. He advised me ahead of time that I would probably "either love it or hate it," but I fell a little short of that. I don't think I'd say I enjoyed it, but it had some interesting parts and the last 1/8 of the book made the rest of it more interesting - like watching the last half hour of The Shawshank Redemption.<br /><br />The basic concept of the book - of Gemma and her son Pietro traveling to Sarajevo so that Pietro can learn more about his father, a photographer who was strongly tied to the city during the brutal war in Bosnia (now Bosnia and Herzegovina) in the early 1990s - was interesting, but the characters chosen to form and tell this story really put me off with their personal choices, right from the start.<br /><br />As the book went on, it got to be increasingly slog-like partly due to the language, which is very lyrical and slightly pretentious. Every time a really obscure word was used, I imagined the translator flipping through a thesaurus trying to pin down the exact word to convey the meaning of the original Italian. I usually avoid even remotely pretentious writing styles, and I honestly don't know how much of it was the original text, and how much was the translation, but it wasn't really my type of novel.<br /><br />I tried not to let that get to me, and just appreciate the storyline, but between the frustrating and off-putting behavior of the characters and the subject matter, I ended up skimming some parts after the halfway point.<br /><br />Things I really, I mean really, just can't or SHOULDN'T read about, because they will pop up in my head for days:<br />- imagery of violence/death involving children<br />- rape<br /><br />Yeah. This book is brutal in its descriptions of the war. I'm not suggesting that books about war SHOULD gloss things over - war is incredibly brutal and we should be reminded how depraved humanity can get sometimes so that we can work harder to prevent it - but since I know this, I've pretty much determined I should stay away from the most graphic descriptions.<br /><br />Soooooo.... I did some skimming during the war scenes. I also did a little more skimming through bits of Gemma and Diego's history that were most frustrating, because I had almost given up on the characters by then. BUT.... then I started reading solidly again about 1/4 of the way from the end, and I'm SO glad I did. There are some really unexpected twists and turns by the end of this novel, and they really change the character of what has gone on before. They are depressing and awful and yet a little tiny bit uplifting at the same time. Diego's story is just ruthlessly awful and goes completely against what I was thinking happened for most of the novel. And this is what saved me from totally disliking the book: the surprises.<br /><br />So, overall: it's pretty long and dragged out, the characters are pretty unlikeable, but the way the author twists the knife at the end makes it a bittersweet story overall and makes me respect her more as an author.<br /><br />It also made me want to learn more about the war in Bosnia... especially since my husband was deployed as part of the UN Peacekeeping force a few years after the war was over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8361809504824270910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review868727586">

<div id="review_306394406" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/306394406" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4079159-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303419720p2/4079159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/306394406?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/4079159-rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer306394406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12884326333934294323">It's been a week since I finished this book, and I can still clearly recall the devastation of Sarajevo and the personalities of the characters. The beautiful writing was poetic and grim. I'll be reading this book again someday.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1053255472" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1053255472" />
    <a title="Aoife" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16768476-aoife"><img alt="Aoife" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514771423p2/16768476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1053255472?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoife" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoife" href="/user/show/16768476-aoife">Aoife</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=historic">historic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=pretty-damn-good">pretty-damn-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=hufflepuff">hufflepuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=survivor-story">survivor-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=literary">literary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=translated">translated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1053255472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7700152089868401481">Oh wow..<br/><br/>This book starts in the 1984 in Bosnia during the Winter Olympics. There, Gemma who is visiting from Italy meets people she will cherish for the rest of her life - Gojko the poet, and Diego the photographer who ends up becoming the love of her life. During their relationship, Diego and Gemma cherish Bosnia as a place where it all started and end up in Sarajevo during the Bosnian War. <br/>16 years later, Gemma returns with her 16-year-old son Pietro, to introduce him to the city he was born i</span>
  <span id="freeText7700152089868401481" style="display:none">Oh wow..<br /><br />This book starts in the 1984 in Bosnia during the Winter Olympics. There, Gemma who is visiting from Italy meets people she will cherish for the rest of her life - Gojko the poet, and Diego the photographer who ends up becoming the love of her life. During their relationship, Diego and Gemma cherish Bosnia as a place where it all started and end up in Sarajevo during the Bosnian War. <br />16 years later, Gemma returns with her 16-year-old son Pietro, to introduce him to the city he was born in - and escaped from at only a few hours old. While revisiting the city of her heart, Gemma is torn between the present and the past, memories of love and of war, and her conflicting emotions and devastating journey of motherhood.<br /><br />CW: Infertility struggles, miscarriage, sexual assault.<br /><br />This book was something else, and I don't think I will forget it for a long, long time. I felt so tense when I was reading this, and I really felt the emotions spilled out onto the pages between Gemma and Diego and all the things said and unsaid between them. The journey in this book - both Gemma's life with Diego and her life with Pietro - is fascinating, and at times it's so hard to watch knowing the disaster that awaits with war on the horizon.<br /><br />The brutality of war is never shied away from in this book, and while it can certainly be hard to figure out why Diego and Gemma stayed in the middle of a war zone when they could travel home to Italy at any time, I still appreciated learning so much about a war that was happening when I was born, and one I know very little about.<br /><br />There is death and destruction in this book that can be hard to read - the death of children playing football or sledding in the snow - picked off like rabbits in a field by snipers on the hill. The death of an old man who was tired of war and walked across a bridge, knowing he would be seen and shot dead. <br /><br />There are also some traumatic and graphic descriptions of rape and sexual assault in this book as a lot of Muslim women were kept in concentration camps and repeatedly raped by soldiers. (Reminder that this only happened less than 30 years ago at the time of writing).<br /><br />Gemma's personal journey of motherhood in this book was so hard to read at times as she suffers from all the highs and lows that come with trying for a baby, and dealing with fertility struggles. Gemma as a character is a hard one to crack to be honest, as a lot of us getting to know her as a reader is through her inner monologue and thoughts rather than actions she takes. There's a lot of times I felt frustrated with her as I felt she was just moving along with the tide, almost blinded by everything except Diego and at times she let herself be a doorstop.<br /><br />I honestly thought I had everyone figured out in this book, and I was honestly raging over characters' decisions and stomping around when the story completely flipped itself and my rage turned to utter despair over the truth of the characters' journeys.<br /><br />There are some wonderful passages in this book, and descriptions of Bosnia and parts of Croatia (Dubrovnik).<br /><br />I do really wish in a way that I could be fluent in Italian and have read this as it was written. I felt the writing style a bit jarring at the start - I believe because of the translation and it took a while for my mind to adapt to the way the story was written in English. I don't think everything came across as beautifully as it probably did in Italian, and there were some passages that read a bit awkwardly.<br /><br />The first 100 pages of this book as well are definitely the hardest to get through as it's mainly just a big build up to Gemma and Diego's life together. Once they are together, the story really begins to flow and then it just becomes utterly addictive.<br /><br />Prepare to sigh at young love, cry in shared grief, rage in despair and finally forgive with compassion alongside these characters.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7700152089868401481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229047359" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229047359" />
    <a title="Margaret" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3717253-margaret"><img alt="Margaret" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332605246p2/3717253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229047359?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaret" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaret" href="/user/show/3717253-margaret">Margaret</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229047359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3153132448518366263">The story of a marriage, of a war, of love. But not a love story by any conventional definition of the term. Gemma and Diego are a mismatched Italian couple who meet in Sarajevo and are drawn back to that city even as the siege is beginning. <br/><br/>The story moves fluidly through time: the present as Gemma takes her son Pietro to Sarajevo to see the city of his birth, and the past as the full story unfolds. <br/><br/>Most than once I almost gave up on the book, as I sensed events unfolding that I didn't want to </span>
  <span id="freeText3153132448518366263" style="display:none">The story of a marriage, of a war, of love. But not a love story by any conventional definition of the term. Gemma and Diego are a mismatched Italian couple who meet in Sarajevo and are drawn back to that city even as the siege is beginning. <br /><br />The story moves fluidly through time: the present as Gemma takes her son Pietro to Sarajevo to see the city of his birth, and the past as the full story unfolds. <br /><br />Most than once I almost gave up on the book, as I sensed events unfolding that I didn't want to read. Have you ever felt that a character you liked was going to disappoint you? I didn't want to experience that, and I felt it was coming. As is my usual practice when I feel like abandoning a book, I read the last few pages to see if I had figured out what was going to happen. I hadn't, and had to go back and finish. <br /><br />The characters, particularly Diego, are complex. I am still trying to figure out how I feel about him. The scenes of war are heartbreaking. The ending is satisfying but as with most good stories, I want to know more. <br /><br />There are some other issues that I would love to talk about but would involve spoilers. There is a lot to this book beyond the plot. If you can handle a story with some very dark moments and pictures of humanity, this is a worthwhile book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3153132448518366263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_214556849" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214556849" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2464996-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246138510p2/2464996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214556849?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/2464996-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214556849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11143568161757451292">Since reading and enjoying Steven Galloway's The Cellist of Sarajevo and The Girl in the Film by Charlotte Eager, I'm irresistibly drawn to novels set around the Bosnian crisis and this one is a corker. The writing is quite superb - matter-of-fact and poetic in its descriptions by turn - sometimes too poetic, but I think that's to do with the translation. The modern story of Gemma's troubled relationship with her teenage son Pietro is well told and engaging through the return to Sarajevo sixteen</span>
  <span id="freeText11143568161757451292" style="display:none">Since reading and enjoying Steven Galloway's The Cellist of Sarajevo and The Girl in the Film by Charlotte Eager, I'm irresistibly drawn to novels set around the Bosnian crisis and this one is a corker. The writing is quite superb - matter-of-fact and poetic in its descriptions by turn - sometimes too poetic, but I think that's to do with the translation. The modern story of Gemma's troubled relationship with her teenage son Pietro is well told and engaging through the return to Sarajevo sixteen years on. The story of the past - her relationship with the photographer Diego, their efforts to have a child, and the dramatic time in Sarajevo are riveting - although the efforts to secure a child were sometimes a little drawn out for my liking. But the start of the siege of Sarajevo - normality falling apart - is incredibly well told. This is a book full of love, passion, family, and it really worked for me. Not the easiest of reads on a number of levels, but really rewarding.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11143568161757451292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1299020918" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1299020918" />
    <a title="Valentina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43680707-valentina"><img alt="Valentina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446925911p2/43680707.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1299020918?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valentina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valentina" href="/user/show/43680707-valentina">Valentina</a>
      </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1299020918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8414695119561483406">4.5/5 <br/><br/>Mazzantini managed to very impressively describe the mentality of the people of former Yugoslavia during both times of war and times of peace from an outsider's perspective. The characters are all very strong, but the character of Gojko really stands out. She also amazingly shows the impact of war on a person's mental health, both through the Italian Gemma and through the Sarajevans.<br/><br/>This book is more philosophical than plot-based, so if you are looking for a quick read, I would not recomme</span>
  <span id="freeText8414695119561483406" style="display:none">4.5/5 <br /><br />Mazzantini managed to very impressively describe the mentality of the people of former Yugoslavia during both times of war and times of peace from an outsider's perspective. The characters are all very strong, but the character of Gojko really stands out. She also amazingly shows the impact of war on a person's mental health, both through the Italian Gemma and through the Sarajevans.<br /><br />This book is more philosophical than plot-based, so if you are looking for a quick read, I would not recommend this. However, if you are looking for a book that will make you think about how hatred impacts innocent lives, this is the book you're looking for.<br /><br />Btw, the movie is great as well! (watch it with subs, because there are three languages used in it: English, Italian and Croatian/Bosnian/Serbian)</span>

<div id="review_344912102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344912102" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6137330-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504542826p2/6137330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344912102?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/6137330-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6137330-lisa?shelf=author-women">author-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6137330-lisa?shelf=translations">translations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6137330-lisa?shelf=fiction-protagonist-women">fiction-protagonist-women</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer344912102&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344912102" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11204879609917956883">Wow! By page 3, this book grabbed me. Mazzantini wields her skill in well-crafted strokes. It is already, one of the books that I am both anxious and reluctant to continue reading. I want very much to get back inside the story--yet if I do, the story will end sooner.<br/><br/>This book kept evolving, but what kept me going back to it was Mazzantini's skill with words and phrases. <br/><br/>By page 100s the story had devolved into yeah-I-was-fucked-up-happily-ever-after story.<br/><br/>By page 200s I have gotten the hang of t</span>
  <span id="freeText11204879609917956883" style="display:none">Wow! By page 3, this book grabbed me. Mazzantini wields her skill in well-crafted strokes. It is already, one of the books that I am both anxious and reluctant to continue reading. I want very much to get back inside the story--yet if I do, the story will end sooner.<br /><br />This book kept evolving, but what kept me going back to it was Mazzantini's skill with words and phrases. <br /><br />By page 100s the story had devolved into yeah-I-was-fucked-up-happily-ever-after story.<br /><br />By page 200s I have gotten the hang of the 16y transitions that flip-flop frequently or so seldom that you are surprised when it happens, which can be mid-chapter. <br /><br />Also, I am losing patience with the main character who stubbornly will not evolve beyond her vanity. She is very self-centered and the love of her life is immature. Their devotion and delight in one another is spoilt by a Gemma's desire to have Diego's child and Diego's desire to be yet another male that aims to give Gemma whatever she wants. She has no daydreams of motherhood. She has thoughts of winding Diego closer to her. <br /><br />Gemma's and Diego's initial trip to Sarajevo was before the outbreak of violence. Diego is there to become a photographer. Gemma is there be a wife. This part of the book is rich while delivering the quintessential life in a European city making friends, in a rare European city unmarked by the World Wars and destination of the 1984 Winter Olympics. The reader gets to be there with the Sarajevo citizens, who discount that the violence breaking out in other places could come to civilized Sarajevo.<br /><br />Gemma had been labelled as a beauty and thus stunted early in life by being attached to a label--not the beauty itself. Gemma's character thus grows to have as much depth as a label. For example, she is the kind of person who joins a gym to workout as her preparation to rejoin a husband in Sarajevo, claiming a firmer physique will make her better able to dodge bullets. <br /><br />Moreover, however much she hungers for introspection she has been blinded by her shallowness. She cannot see that she is trying to compete with a young girl she paid to be a surrogate and whom she believes is now loved by her husband. It is Diego who redirects her return trip preparations from the ego-centric to what is really needed in Sarajevo: suitcases filled with as many provisions as she can carry. <br /><br />Gemma is also the kind of person who when feeling neglected can destroy Diegos photographs, reasoning what else could she do with her feelings of displacement. Diego,on the other hand, has matured during her absence. We find out in the end he confronted his weakness, then worked as the person he wanted to become. Those photos, for example, were of siege survivors, who requested that Diego photograph them so that there would be proof to family and friends elsewhere that they continued to survive the siege. <br /><br />Gemma's redeeming quality is that she knows that she is shallow and lacking. <br /><br />On the upside, what glued me to Manzantini's story was the storytelling and Sarajevo.<br /><br />By page 300s I wondering how I can stand to read a 10 page account of sniper targeting a child that starts then starts again and again after another thread of the story interrupts...or is it that the telling of this crime cannot be sustained. Does horror make what comes next indiscernible, well at least until I have a moment to walk away from it, which is unlike people trapped inside war. So, I am watching myself read this horrible stuff--me who walks out of violent movies and cannot abide by any joke that is cruel. Yet, I am reading about life and living being taken without cause without reason, just because it can be done. How can I? I am stunned to realize that the author has slowly and irradically been turning up the heat, so that I like a frog being boiled to death--I do not jump out. I have become like some of the citizens of Sarajevo, who thought with certainty that things would not get very bad.<br /><br />By page 400s I question whether Gemma is the main character. Also, I know that I what I suspected 50pages earlier has to be "the twist", if not I would be deeply dissapointed in this writer's ability to use her craft to convey a truth. I also have come to accept that it will not be the main character who will be Twice Born. Despite her declared bravery taking off in a UN plane, within hours she has met her next rescuer, in the form of her future husband. Oh well, I think--no big transformation for this protagonist. So I settle myself into reading for the big climax (i.e. the twist) that is due to come any page now. <br /><br />At the ending my eyes filled with bittersweet tears. Someone is Twice Born and the twist was not climax. Manzantini's story is high art. <br /><br />This is a difficult story, because war is difficult. Here is a way you might know whether you are up for this story at this time. East of Eden, by Steinbeck has a beautiful self-contained story within the novel, that I found otherwise tedious. Read the story about a Chinese laborer working on the Continental Railroad. If you can love that story, you can love this story. Both are sublime. This one is longer and requires more endurance from the reader.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11204879609917956883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_858589722" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858589722" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/858589722?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yuliana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yuliana" href="/user/show/4585490-yuliana">Yuliana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4585490-yuliana?shelf=best-books-of-all-times">best-books-of-all-times</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer858589722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16943908661749951542">This book left me breathless. It gripped me from the first page and didn’t let go until the very last page. It crawled under my skin, penetrated my mind; I breathed it, lived it, dreamt it. It crossed my path at the right time, when I started experiencing personal growth and rethinking and re-evaluating my life, beliefs. <br/>This book was like an unexpected blow to my head that knocked me senseless...or maybe knocked some sense into me. It crept inside me, turned me inside out, leaving me raw with w</span>
  <span id="freeText16943908661749951542" style="display:none">This book left me breathless. It gripped me from the first page and didn’t let go until the very last page. It crawled under my skin, penetrated my mind; I breathed it, lived it, dreamt it. It crossed my path at the right time, when I started experiencing personal growth and rethinking and re-evaluating my life, beliefs. <br />This book was like an unexpected blow to my head that knocked me senseless...or maybe knocked some sense into me. It crept inside me, turned me inside out, leaving me raw with wonder about life and myself.<br />This book is not an easy read. It requires guts to stick to its brutal honesty, fierce language and vulnerable characters. This book is a life lesson which I am starting to learn - live my life with untamed passion; give in to unconditional love in its most unexpected form; open my mind; follow my heart; do what I think is right and not what others think; be kind to others and myself; embrace life and its challenges. This book teaches me to live. Maybe that’s why I am so reluctant to put it down. But it’s time to let go and start my own story, weave its plot with kindness and passion; I already have a wonderful set of characters awaiting me.<br />Good luck. Enjoy. Absorb or get absorbed. You won’t regret it. The only thing you will regret is that the book is finished. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16943908661749951542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_804100808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/804100808" />
    <a title="Danka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5484568-danka"><img alt="Danka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383215513p2/5484568.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/804100808?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danka" href="/user/show/5484568-danka">Danka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer804100808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7951350553492661820">Wow... This is one of those books that grab you and never let you go! It's beautiful and fascinating, but schocking and awfully tragic at the same time. Reading about the devastation and siege of Sarajevo, that wonderful and unique town, back in 1990s tortured me throughout the book, yet I kept reading and I couldn't stop. If anyone has ever thought a war might be justified, they will change their opinion after reading this book. There is nothing more tragic and more wrong than a war-torn countr</span>
  <span id="freeText7951350553492661820" style="display:none">Wow... This is one of those books that grab you and never let you go! It's beautiful and fascinating, but schocking and awfully tragic at the same time. Reading about the devastation and siege of Sarajevo, that wonderful and unique town, back in 1990s tortured me throughout the book, yet I kept reading and I couldn't stop. If anyone has ever thought a war might be justified, they will change their opinion after reading this book. There is nothing more tragic and more wrong than a war-torn country with hundreds of thousands of former brothers and sisters killing and tormenting each other for no other reason but politics and twisted ideas of a bunch of lunatics. Margret Mazzantini managed to portray this absurdity in a wonderfully realistic yet poetic way. The characters are realistic and well-developed, love stories are beautiful without being melodramatic and the town of Sarajevo is the real hero of the book - it managed to heal, forgive if not forget and it stands as a symbol of all the other towns and people that were destroyed or fatally wounded in that tragic and absurd war. <br />This is a book you keep thinking about long after you finish reading it. It's highly recommendable, but you need to be in the right mood for it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7951350553492661820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_501992733" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/501992733" />
    <a title="Simon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/745423-simon"><img alt="Simon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527235428p2/745423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/501992733?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simon" href="/user/show/745423-simon">Simon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788804573708" href="/book/show/6202353-venuto-al-mondo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/745423-simon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/745423-simon?shelf=italian">italian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer501992733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer157806157316858222">Glad I finally made it through this, as I was struggling at times but it was worth it in the end.<br/>The vocabulary was pretty rich for my level of Italian, which may have put me off a little, but I also felt it was too long and rambling. Mazzantini also likes to hit you over the head with metaphors (in a story about fertility the egg imagery was a bit much) and the Ivo Andrić story about the goat and the wolf is leaned on pretty heavily.<br/>However the story is involving and finally moving, and even if</span>
  <span id="freeText157806157316858222" style="display:none">Glad I finally made it through this, as I was struggling at times but it was worth it in the end.<br />The vocabulary was pretty rich for my level of Italian, which may have put me off a little, but I also felt it was too long and rambling. Mazzantini also likes to hit you over the head with metaphors (in a story about fertility the egg imagery was a bit much) and the Ivo Andrić story about the goat and the wolf is leaned on pretty heavily.<br />However the story is involving and finally moving, and even if you don't like the characters (personally I found Diego infuriating at times) you at least understand them and the choices they make. In fact the whole story is about personal choices, and how they are sometimes forced on us by circumstances beyond our control.<br />Avoid the trailer for the recent film version, which gives away most of the plot (apart from the final twist) in the space of two minutes.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15450074894758375273">I won this through a goodreads giveaway. And it is the paperback version. It is also an Advance Uncorrected Proof; so there were a few spellings and punctuation problems but nothing major.<br/><br/>What can I say about this book? It's beautiful. Translated from Italian, it is a slow, deep read. I'm usually a fast reader but this book wouldn't let me go through it quickly. It demands a paced, calm reading.   <span id="freeText15450074894758375273" style="display:none">I won this through a goodreads giveaway. And it is the paperback version. It is also an Advance Uncorrected Proof; so there were a few spellings and punctuation problems but nothing major.<br /><br />What can I say about this book? It's beautiful. Translated from Italian, it is a slow, deep read. I'm usually a fast reader but this book wouldn't let me go through it quickly. It demands a paced, calm reading. It demands the depths that the language provides. Beautiful, poetic language. The story is heartbreaking with hope at the end. It's a war book. A love story. A motherhood story. A journey. It is a lot of things all wrapped up into one.<br /><br />This book isn't my usual style, it isn't something I would normally pick up and read but I am incredibly glad that I won it because it was well worth the read. <br /><br />Absolutely beautiful. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166114995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13181367080874482310">This was an incredible book! I won it from Goodreads, and was so glad that I did because this book is just so sophisticated and beautifully written. It is the story of an Italian woman and her Serajevan husband who are unable to conceive due to infertility. The book takes you on their journey through flashbacks detailing their life together, as well as the woman's personal journey years after the war. The book takes place in both Italy and Sarajevo during the war and afterwards.It is fiction, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText13181367080874482310" style="display:none">This was an incredible book! I won it from Goodreads, and was so glad that I did because this book is just so sophisticated and beautifully written. It is the story of an Italian woman and her Serajevan husband who are unable to conceive due to infertility. The book takes you on their journey through flashbacks detailing their life together, as well as the woman's personal journey years after the war. The book takes place in both Italy and Sarajevo during the war and afterwards.It is fiction, but it is so real and raw--it is just heartbreaking in some parts. This is a story that uncovers what it is like to love another person, what it is like to live through the violence and tragedy of war, what it means to be a human being. I was just so impressed by this author's writing! The book is an international bestseller, and it is easy to see why. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13181367080874482310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11293193555414121949">I expected to enjoy this book as much as I enjoyed "Don't Move" by the same author, but my anticipation has been deceived. Mrs. Mazzantini elaborates too much on little unnecessary details that in my opinion distract the reader's attention from the incomplete characters she has created. The narrator is too pathetic, I could barely stand her. The writing style is too chaotic, the story line too predictable. <br/>This is one of those rare occasions where I liked the movie better than the book just beca</span>
  <span id="freeText11293193555414121949" style="display:none">I expected to enjoy this book as much as I enjoyed "Don't Move" by the same author, but my anticipation has been deceived. Mrs. Mazzantini elaborates too much on little unnecessary details that in my opinion distract the reader's attention from the incomplete characters she has created. The narrator is too pathetic, I could barely stand her. The writing style is too chaotic, the story line too predictable. <br />This is one of those rare occasions where I liked the movie better than the book just because all that excessive drama is avoided and Gemma (Penelope Cruz) is not as piteous as it sounds in the novel. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1682215404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2246924469633801487">A haunting, breathtaking drama set against the backdrop of the siege of Sarajevo, this book will stay with me for a long time. I had to keep reminding myself that this was not a memoir, because although translated from Italian and told in a beautiful, although sometimes overly poetical tone it is still very believable. The plot is very well developed and has some unexpected twists that left me almost wanting to reread the whole book to have an even better understanding of the characters. This is</span>
  <span id="freeText2246924469633801487" style="display:none">A haunting, breathtaking drama set against the backdrop of the siege of Sarajevo, this book will stay with me for a long time. I had to keep reminding myself that this was not a memoir, because although translated from Italian and told in a beautiful, although sometimes overly poetical tone it is still very believable. The plot is very well developed and has some unexpected twists that left me almost wanting to reread the whole book to have an even better understanding of the characters. This is a story that leaves one with lots to think about. A very absorbing story that I found hard to put down.<br />I would like to give this 4.5 stars.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137247545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4039907264181484654">A great, intriguing book about the vagaries of war - internal and external. It is set in both Italy and Sarajevo (during the war) and involves a young couple who discover that they cannot have children due to the woman's infertility. This sets in motion a very difficult period in their lives that is rooted in the violence of the war riddled streets of Sarajevo. Beautifully written but a long journey! I am almost finished. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline Petruzzi McHale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline Petruzzi McHale" href="/user/show/3286488-caroline-petruzzi-mchale">Caroline Petruzzi McHale</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1284478616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3721114839178448966">Ouf. I bought this book about three years ago, after finishing Elena Ferrante's My Beautiful Friend and the three remaining books in the series. I must have stumbled upon a list of "If you like Ferrante..." This book shares a few things with Ferrante (Italy, themes of identity and motherhood), but it's more complex and I find myself preferring Mazzantini to Ferrante (never thought she could be outdone, but...) It's one of those books with many lives - you think will be about one thing, then you </span>
  <span id="freeText3721114839178448966" style="display:none">Ouf. I bought this book about three years ago, after finishing Elena Ferrante's My Beautiful Friend and the three remaining books in the series. I must have stumbled upon a list of "If you like Ferrante..." This book shares a few things with Ferrante (Italy, themes of identity and motherhood), but it's more complex and I find myself preferring Mazzantini to Ferrante (never thought she could be outdone, but...) It's one of those books with many lives - you think will be about one thing, then you discover it's actually about something entirely different and then it concludes even further from where you thought it was going. It's a beautiful tribute to some very heavy topics. I feel enriched but also even more confused about war and specifically the Balkan conflict, which is chronicled to some extent in the book. Mazzantini gets major points for nailing references to Bruce Springsteen and Vasco Rossi (the Italian Bruce Springsteen) in the book. "Voglio trovare un senso a questa vita... Anche se questa vita un senso non ce l'ha..." 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3721114839178448966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('haNUq4bIVIZ5lyyE8Jxi3qHQIBblNTRns6R+I8UBPTWEsiMlSGLmCUtCbBiF6gzCEZSc5AruiRWOoYf5QAokSw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Attraverso lo sguardo privilegiato della bambina che cresce, le contraddizioni tra il vecchio e il nuovo emergono via via piú evidenti: nell’esperienza della scuola dell’obbligo, e in quella del confronto tra la fede cristiana e i retaggi di una religiosità assai piú antica nel tempo. Donatella Di Pietrantonio conosce le parole per dirlo, e affronta il tema della maternità, della responsabilità e della cura, da una prospettiva originale e con una rara intensità espressiva. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11448788422693761333">Margaret Mazzantini is an Italian writer and actress. She became a film, television and stage actor, but is best known as a writer. Mazzantini began her acting career in 1980 starring in the cult horror classic Antropophagus, she has also appeared in television and theatre. As a successful writer her novels include Non ti muovere (Don't Move) which was adapted into a film of the same name and is d</span>
  <span id="freeText11448788422693761333" style="display:none">Margaret Mazzantini is an Italian writer and actress. She became a film, television and stage actor, but is best known as a writer. Mazzantini began her acting career in 1980 starring in the cult horror classic Antropophagus, she has also appeared in television and theatre. As a successful writer her novels include Non ti muovere (Don't Move) which was adapted into a film of the same name and is directed by her husband Sergio Castellitto and stars Penélope Cruz. Her career as a writer and actress has earned her several awards and nominations including Campiello Awards, a Golden Ticket Award, and a Goya Award. She married Sergio Castellitto in 1987. They have four children. She lives in Rome.</span>
